Roughly two and a half hours from anywhere you've heard of. Close enough to the Davis Mountains to see them on a clear day, far enough from the interstate that you have to mean to get there.\nPopulation: 1,204 (the sign has said 1,204 for eleven years; nobody has updated it)\nFounded: 1887, as a stop on a cattle drive route\nClimate: Bone-dry, wind-scoured, brutal summers, mild winters, spring bluebonnets, the occasional dust storm that blots out the sun\nEconomy: Ranching, a small oil services company, the diner, the feed store, a handful of tourists in spring who come for the wildflowers\nKey Locations:\nTHE LANTERN RANCH — Brennan family land, four generations. Northeast of town, about twelve minutes out on a county road. (Full section below.)\nTHE LANTERN CAFÉ — Maeve's diner. Main Street. Open 5 AM to 2 PM, closed Mondays. Same lantern on the sign as on the ranch gate. Booths upholstered in cracked red vinyl. Pie case visible from every seat. The unofficial town hall, courtroom, and confessional.\nTHE OLD RODEO GROUNDS — Southwest edge of town. Arena, grandstand, stables, stock pens. Has not hosted an event in ten years. The arena is still mostly standing; the stables burned and were never rebuilt. Kids dare each other to walk through it at night. Wyatt has not been inside the fence in a decade.\nDELANEY VETERINARY CLINIC — Main Street, two doors down from the café. Doc's name is still on the door. Wren will repaint it.\nMAIN STREET — One stoplight (broken since '09, functions as a four-way stop that everyone treats as a suggestion). The café, the clinic, the feed store, Sutton's Hardware, a post office, a Baptist church, a Methodist church (they do not speak), a bar called THE BRANDING IRON where Rhett bartends, a defunct movie theater someone keeps threatening to restore.\nDOC DELANEY'S HOUSE — A blue clapboard two-story on a side street, three blocks off Main. Porch swing. Rose bushes his late wife planted. Doc still deadheads them every Sunday.\nTHE HIGH SCHOOL — Hart's Ridge Combined (K-12, because the population can't justify two buildings). Mascot: the Ridgebacks.\nTHE CHURCH(ES) & THE SHERIFF — One sheriff, name Tommy Shultz, probably sixty-something, went to school with Hank, attends Sunday pot roast approximately twice a year.\n3. THE LANTERN RANCH\nHistory: Established 1889 by Eliza Brennan, a widow who inherited her husband's land claim and refused to sell it. She hung a lantern on the front gate every night to guide her ranch hands home from the far pastures. Her daughter did the same. Her granddaughter. Her great-granddaughter — MAEVE BRENNAN — married HANK HOLLOWAY in 1988 and added his name to the gate but kept hers on the deed. The Brennan women have worked this land for 136 years.\nThe Lantern: A cast-iron carriage lantern, original to the homestead. Hangs from the crossbeam of the front gate. Was lit every night from 1889 to the night of the fire. Has not been lit since. Maeve walks past it every morning and does not look at it.\nLayout:\nMain House — Two-story Victorian farmhouse, white clapboard, wraparound porch. Maeve lives here alone now. Four bedrooms upstairs (the boys' old rooms, mostly preserved). Kitchen is the heart of the house; always something on the stove.\nThe Barn — Large working barn, 1920s, recently reinforced. Hayloft. Tack room. Stalls for the working horses.\nThe Barn Apartment — Converted hayloft space above the barn's west end. Has its own exterior staircase. Small — one bedroom, small kitchen, a bathtub under a window that looks out at the pasture. Hasn't been rented in years. Maeve cleaned it herself.\nThe Horse Barn — Separate structure, newer, for the rodeo stock that survived. Jesse's domain.\nWyatt's House — A smaller ranch house about a quarter mile from the main house. Wyatt moved out of the main house three years after the fire. It's deliberately spare.\nJesse's Cabin — A one-room cabin near the horse barn. He built it himself at nineteen. Nobody goes in.\nSamuel's Cabin — On the far edge of the property, near the creek. Further than Jesse's. More deliberate.\nRhett — Does NOT live on the ranch. Has an apartment above the Branding Iron.\nCaleb — Has not lived on the ranch in ten years. His room in the main house is exactly as he left it at twenty-two.\n4. THE HOLLOWAY FAMILY\nHANK HOLLOWAY (1962–died 10 years ago, age ~52)\nThe Ghost. Rodeo legend across three counties. Built like a barn, laugh like a thunderclap, could calm a bucking bronc by humming to it. Married Maeve Brennan at twenty-six; never looked at another woman. Called his five boys \"the herd.\" Loved them fiercely and told them almost never. Had a temper he kept mostly in check. Stubborn as weather. Emotionally buttoned-up in the specific West Texas way of his generation — love was shown in actions, in showing up, in fixing things without being asked.\nSignature: Tipped his hat to Maeve every time he left the house and said, \"Back before the stars, darlin'.\"\nThe Fight: Morning of the fire, fought with Wyatt about vet school. Told him a Holloway man works the land. Wyatt said, \"I hope I never turn into you.\" Hank left without tipping his hat. It was the only time in thirty-two years of marriage he forgot.\nThe Last Words to Jesse: Pulled him aside before his ride, said, \"I'm proud of you, son. You're gonna be something.\"\nDeath: Ran back into the burning stables for the horses. Got three out. Did not come out himself.\nMAEVE BRENNAN HOLLOWAY (age ~60)\nThe Matriarch. Owner of the land, owner of the diner, owner of more information than any person in Hart's Ridge. Warm, shrewd, unsentimental in the face of sentiment. Widowed at fifty, raised five grown sons through grief by feeding them. Runs the Lantern Café six days a week and has for thirty years. Has not watched a sunset from the porch in ten years.\nAppearance: Silver in her dark hair, laugh lines, hands that are always doing something. Favors jeans and soft flannel shirts at home, an apron at the diner.\nSignature: The pies. (See Section 8.)\nThe Secret: Somewhere around Year Six, she figured out what Jesse did. She has never said a word. She is waiting for him to say it first.\nHer Authority: The boys do not fully understand that their mother is the landowner. They think they run the ranch. They do not.\nWYATT HOLLOWAY (34) — BOOK 1\nThe Dutiful One. Oldest brother. Runs The Lantern Ranch. Wanted to be a vet; wasn't allowed to finish the conversation with his father about it. Became Hank instead, on purpose, as penance.\nAppearance: 6'3\", built from labor not gym. Dark hair, dark eyes, perpetual two-day stubble. Hands that have stitched barbed wire and calved cows. Wears Wranglers and work shirts, same Stetson for eight years.\nWound: Fought with Hank the morning of the fire. Said \"I hope I never turn into you.\" Has been becoming him ever since.\nArmor: Grumpiness. Silence. Work.\nWhat Wren Sees: The boy who wanted to be a vet, still in there.\nTrope: Grumpy/sunshine + forced proximity.\nArc: From penance to permission.\nCALEB HOLLOWAY (32) — BOOK 2\nThe Runaway. Second son. Left Hart's Ridge three weeks after the funeral and became a circuit rodeo star out of Las Vegas. Famous enough that Hart's Ridge sees his face on the rare TV in the Branding Iron and pretends not to. Has not been home in ten years.\nAppearance: Leaner than Wyatt, more camera-ready, the brother who inherited Hank's laugh. Shaggier hair. Wears his buckle.\nWound: Guilt. He left. He left his mother, he left the ranch, he left the girl he loved, and he's been trying to outrun all three on eight-second rides.\nArmor: Distance. Charm. The next arena.\nTrope: Second chance romance.\nHeroine: His high school sweetheart, now a single mom. Name: Nora Henshaw.\nBook 1 Presence: Off-page until the final scene. Headlights in the driveway. Engine cut. Door opens.\nSAMUEL HOLLOWAY (30) — BOOK 3\nThe Angry One. Middle brother. Was nineteen when the fire happened and the year at college that was supposed to come next never did. Enlisted instead. Served two tours. Came home harder than he left. Lives alone in the cabin by the creek.\nAppearance: The broodingest of the five. Shorter hair, military-neat. A scar on his jaw he will not talk about. Broader than Caleb, quieter than Wyatt.\nWound: Rage he has nowhere to put. A private theory about the fire he has told no one. The thing he saw, or thinks he saw, that night.\nArmor: Solitude. Whiskey. The cabin.\nTrope: Enemies to lovers.\nHeroine: Arson investigator reopening the case. Name: Isabel Esquivel.\nBook 1 Presence: Shows up for Sunday dinner. Says maybe fourteen words the whole book. All of them matter.\nRHETT HOLLOWAY (28) — BOOK 4\nThe Charmer. Fourth brother. Bartends at the Branding Iron. Everyone's friend, nobody's problem. Lives above the bar. Looks like he's not carrying anything.\nAppearance: Golden-retriever energy, dimples, the brother who makes women laugh before they realize they're flirting. Lighter hair than the others, blue eyes from Maeve's side.\nWound: Avoidance. If he never takes anything seriously, nothing can break him. Was eighteen when the fire happened. Has never once cried about it out loud.\nArmor: The joke. The smile. The next round.\nTrope: Fake dating + one bed.\nHeroine: Caleb's disgraced Vegas ex, hiding out in Hart's Ridge.\nBook 1 Presence: Easy. Teases Wyatt about Wren within four hours of her arrival. Is always at Sunday dinner. Is the brother most visibly delighted by the Wren situation.\nJESSE HOLLOWAY (26) — BOOK 5\nThe Quiet One. Baby of the family. Was sixteen the night of the fire. Flicked a cigarette into dry grass behind the rodeo grounds trying to feel grown. Walked away. Watched his father ride. Figured out what he'd done days later, alone, in his bedroom, and never told a soul.\nAppearance: Tallest of the brothers, actually — grew late. Lean, quiet hands, dark hair always a little too long because he forgets. Moves softer than a man his size should.\nWound: He killed his father. He believes this without qualification. He has carried it for a decade.\nArmor: Silence. Work. Proximity to the animals Hank died for.\nTrope: Forbidden age-gap, friends-to-lovers.\nHeroine: His former high school English teacher, back in town. Name: Holly Lovett.\nBook 1 Presence: On-page but quiet. Six specific seed moments (see Lila's list above, Section 7 will formalize).\n5. THE DELANEY FAMILY\nDOC DELANEY (mid-60s)\nFirst name RAY. Hank's best friend since they were eight years old. Hart's Ridge's town vet for thirty-five years. Widowed when Wren was fourteen (her mother, Martha Delaney, died of cancer — off-page, long pre-series). Identified Hank's body after the fire. Has never fully come back from that Tuesday.\nAppearance: White hair, sun-wrinkled, gentle hands. Looks like a man carved out of the Texas landscape.\nRole: Platonic co-conspirator to Maeve. Sunday pot roast at the Lantern Ranch, every week, for ten years. Second father to the Holloway boys.\nArc in Series: Quiet, supportive, occasionally devastating with a one-liner at the right moment. Appears in every book. Does not die.\nWREN DELANEY, DVM (28)\nBOOK 1 HEROINE. Only child of Doc and Martha Delaney. Grew up in Hart's Ridge. Left for college at eighteen, vet school after. Worked in Dallas emergency medicine until a bad night two years ago. Quietly broke. Spent two weeks with her dad, then moved to a rental two counties over and rebuilt herself on her own terms at a large-animal practice. Now taking over her father's Hart's Ridge clinic.\nAppearance: 5'5\", curvy-soft, honey-brown hair usually in a practical braid with flyaways, freckles that show in summer. Aesthetic: Anthropologie catalog but make it manure-proof. Floral sundresses over jeans, an embroidered Carhartt, cowboy boots from Etsy that aren't quite right.\nWound: Lost a patient in Dallas after a triple shift. Family was devastated. She broke quietly over six months. Doc packed her apartment in a weekend.\nArmor: Chosen sunshine. Humming while she makes coffee. Florals with the overalls. Every bright thing is a small act of defiance.\nWhat Wyatt Sees: Not the girl in pigtails. Not anymore.\nVehicle: Beat-up Subaru Outback. Dog hair she doesn't own a dog for. Granola bars in the console. A stethoscope in the passenger seat.\n6. SUPPORTING CAST\nTHE LANTERN CAFÉ STAFF:\nGRANT — fry cook, age 50s, has worked there twenty years, says maybe three words a shift.\nBIRDIE — waitress, age 70s, knows your order, your ex, and your credit score. Calls everyone \"sugar.\" Has a running bet with herself about when Wyatt will kiss Wren. (She wins in chapter 18.)\nTHE BRANDING IRON:\nRhett tends. Owner is an old-timer named GIBBS who mostly lets Rhett run it.\nNEIGHBORS & RIVALS:\nTHE McKINNEY FAMILY — Neighboring ranch. Hank's old rodeo rivals-turned-friends. [BUILD OUT AS NEEDED — a McKinney daughter or son could surface in a later book.]\nTHE SHERIFF:\nTommy Shultz — Went to school with Hank. Sixty-something. Will matter in Book 3.\nPIVOTAL TO BOOK 2:\nCaleb's high school sweetheart, Nora — lives in town, is a single mom, per Edna's rule, kid's dad is a man who left, who we hate.\nHer child — age, gender, name TBD.\n7. THE FIRE — SERIES MYSTERY BIBLE SACRED DOCUMENT\nWHAT ACTUALLY HAPPENED, IN FULL:\nTen years ago, the second weekend of July. Annual Hart's Ridge Summer Rodeo — the biggest event of the year, the thing the town organized itself around. Hank Holloway competing, as he did every year. All five boys there. Maeve working the pie booth.\nThat afternoon, Wyatt (24) and Hank fought in the kitchen about vet school. Wyatt said the cruel thing, slammed the door, went to the rodeo angry and stayed at the arena fence drinking beer with friends.\nCaleb (22) was competing too, in his father's shadow.\nSamuel (20) was home from his first year of college, surly, not really speaking to Hank for reasons of his own (the real reasons are Book 3's reveal — he'd applied to enlist without telling anyone, and Hank had found out).\nRhett (18) was flirting with everyone and drinking beer he wasn't supposed to have.\nJesse (16) was the baby brother tagging along. Before Hank's ride, Hank pulled Jesse aside and said, \"I'm proud of you, son. You're gonna be something.\" Jesse, overwhelmed and sixteen and trying to be bigger than he was, stole a cigarette from an older kid's pack and slipped behind the stables to smoke it. He inhaled wrong, coughed, panicked someone would hear, and flicked the cigarette into the dry grass at the base of the stable wall. Walked away. Went back to watch his dad ride. Never saw it catch.\nIt smoldered for maybe forty minutes. The stable wall caught during Hank's final ride. By the time anyone noticed, the wind had it. Hank rode out of the arena, saw the smoke, and went for the horses. Got three out. A beam came down. He did not come out.\nOfficial cause: undetermined. Likely electrical (old wiring). The investigation was cursory. The town was in shock. Nobody looked hard.\nJesse realized four days later, lying in bed, replaying that night. He has told no one. For ten years.\nTHE BROTHERS' PRIVATE THEORIES (what each one secretly believes):\nWyatt: Believes the fight distracted Hank, made him ride sloppy, put him in the wrong place at the wrong time. Believes he killed his father with words.\nCaleb: Believes if he'd won his event earlier, Hank wouldn't have stayed for the later ride. Believes he killed his father by losing.\nSamuel: Saw something that night — a figure near the stables before the fire. Never identified them. Has spent ten years wondering if it was arson, if someone hated Hank enough, and if he, Samuel, failed to protect his father by not walking over to check. (Reveal Book 3: the figure was Jesse.)\nRhett: Believes nothing. Refuses to. That's the wound.\nJesse: Knows.\nMaeve: Figured it out in Year Six. A moment with Jesse, a look, something she put together. Has been waiting for him.\nTHE CONTROLLED REVEAL SCHEDULE:\nBOOK 1 (WYATT):\nEmotional reveal: Wyatt tells Wren what he said to Hank that morning.\nPlanted seeds: Jesse stopped talking for a year. Jesse doesn't drink. Jesse tends the horses. Jesse reacts to the cigarette at the test-run rodeo. Maeve watches Jesse leave dinner. The lantern is mentioned but not lit.\nBOOK 2 (CALEB):\nEmotional reveal: Caleb confesses why he really left — not just grief, but the belief that losing cost his father his life.\nPlanted seeds: Jesse's avoidance of the old rodeo grounds becomes specific. A conversation where Jesse almost says something and doesn't. Maeve bakes something unusual when Jesse walks into the café.\nBOOK 3 (SAMUEL):\nEmotional reveal: Samuel tells the arson investigator about the figure he saw that night. She investigates. The trail goes cold on paper but the reader knows. First major \"oh God\" for attentive rereaders.\nPlanted seeds: Jesse reacts when the investigator is mentioned. A near-miss where he almost tells her himself.\nBOOK 4 (RHETT):\nEmotional reveal: Rhett finally breaks. Cries about Hank for the first time. In the cry, he says something like \"I keep thinking one of us knows something and isn't saying.\" The heroine holds him.\nPlanted seeds: Jesse drinks for the first time on-page. One drink. Sets it down. Walks out of the bar. Rhett notices.\nBOOK 5 (JESSE):\nThe confession. To his teacher-heroine first. Then, in the climax, to all four brothers and Maeve. Then Maeve slides the pie across the table. \"I've been waiting, baby.\" The lantern is lit.\n8. MAEVE'S PIE LEXICON\nThe official pie dictionary. Tight list, series-wide consistency.\nPie\nMeaning\nApple\nPleased. All is well. The default.\nLemon Meringue\nSomeone's about to get their life rearranged.\nCherry\nWarning. Tread carefully.\nPecan\nGrief. Unspoken sorrow.\nKey Lime\nShe knows something you don't.\nPeach\nWelcome home.\nButtermilk Chess\nForgiveness. (The Book 5 pie. Never appears before.)\n9. SERIES MOTIFS & RECURRING ELEMENTS\nThe Lantern on the Gate — Unlit for ten years. Mentioned in every book. Lit in Book 5.\n\"Back before the stars, darlin'.\" — Hank's signature. Appears in every book. Maeve says it aloud for the first time in ten years at a key moment in Book 5.\nThe Broken Stoplight — Running gag. Fixed in Book 5. Nobody likes it.\nSunday Pot Roast — Maeve's house, every week, attendance mandatory. Every book has at least one pot roast scene.\nMaeve's Pies — every book opens OR climaxes with a specific pie call.\nThe Old Rodeo Grounds — Appears in every book. Different character goes there each time. Book 5, all five brothers go together.\nDoc's Porch Swing — Confession location. Every book has a scene on it.\nThe Empty Chair — Hank's chair at the kitchen table. Nobody sits in it. Ever. Until Book 5.\n10. TIMELINE\n1889: Eliza Brennan establishes the ranch.\n1988: Maeve Brennan marries Hank Holloway.\n1990–2000: The five boys arrive: Wyatt ('90), Caleb ('92), Samuel ('94), Rhett ('96), Jesse ('98).\n10 Years Before Series: The Fire. Hank dies. Jesse is 16.\nSeries Present (Book 1): Spring-Summer. Wyatt 34, Caleb 32 (absent), Samuel 30, Rhett 28, Jesse 26.\nBook 2: Autumn of same year.\nBook 3: Following year. Next season. Winter.\nBook 4: Following year. Next Season. Spring.\nBook 5: The next summer. Full rodeo revival — ten-year anniversary reframed as commemoration and rebirth.\n11. THEMATIC THROUGH-LINES\nInherited silence. Five sons raised by a man who loved in actions; none of them know the words.\nMatrilineal land, patrilineal grief. The ranch belongs to the women. The wound belongs to the men.\nHome as wound and healing. Hart's Ridge is where it broke and the only place it can mend.\nPenance vs. permission. Every brother has been punishing himself. Every love interest offers permission.\nThe story you tell yourself vs. the truth. Each brother has built a private narrative of that night. Love is what makes the truth sayable.\nChosen joy. Not innocence, not denial — joy as an active, daily decision. (Wren's thesis. The series' thesis.)\n12. BRAND & MARKETING ANCHORS\nSeries Branding:\nUnified cover motif: A silhouetted figure under the ranch gate, lantern hanging above. Same lantern, different brother, different heroine silhouette, book title in weathered serif. Spine features the lantern. Five books on a shelf = one lantern glowing in sequence.\nColor palette: Dusty neutrals, rust, Texas sky blue, amber. Book 5 introduces lantern-gold.\nSeries tagline: Back before the stars.\nTrope Bingo per Book:\nBook\nPrimary\nSecondary\nTertiary\n1 Wyatt\nGrumpy/Sunshine\nForced Proximity\n(father) Brother's Best Friend's Daughter\n2 Caleb\nSecond Chance\nSingle Mom\nProdigal Son Returns\n3 Samuel\nEnemies to Lovers\nWounded Veteran\nForbidden (Professional)\n4 Rhett\nFake Dating\nOne Bed\nBrother's Ex\n5 Jesse\nAge Gap\nForbidden (Teacher)\nFriends to Lovers + Mystery Resolution\nNewsletter Magnet / Pre-Order Bonus: \"BACK BEFORE THE STARS\" — A novella of Hank and Maeve, young. How they met. Their wedding. The first time he said the line. Releases between Book 4 and Book 5. Devastates everyone.\nMerch Ecosystem:\nLantern pillar candle (leather & smoke)\nThe Lantern Café recipe card set (Maeve's pies, one per book, included as special-edition inserts)\n\"Back before the stars\" enamel pin\nHart's Ridge map print\nBranded Carhartt (Wren-coded)\nTarget Reader: Elsie Silver, Lyla Sage, Tessa Bailey, Robyn Carr. BookTok-native. 25–45. Reads in series. Owns a tote bag. Will pre-order Book 2 the day Book 1 releases if we nail the ending.\n\nThe author's pen name is Lillie Rose Hart.\n\nBooks in this series:\n- Back Before The Stars: "

As the oldest brother, he took the reins of the struggling Lantern Ranch after the fire that killed his father, abandoning his own dream of becoming a veterinarian to shoulder the family’s grief. He’s become a man of stone, work, and silence, convinced that his final, angry words to his father are what truly caused the tragedy. He doesn't have room in his life for anything but penance—until Wren Delaney pulls back into town in a beat-up Subaru filled with dog hair and defiant optimism.\n\nThe Conflict: Wren, the local vet’s daughter, is returning to Hart’s Ridge to take over her father’s clinic, carrying her own quiet trauma from a tragic loss in Dallas. When she ends up renting the Barn Apartment right on Wyatt's property, their forced proximity is a clash of grumpy-meets-sunshine. Wren wears floral sundresses over manure-stained overalls and hums while she works, driving Wyatt absolutely crazy—and making him feel things he swore he’d buried forever. As they are forced to work side-by-side to save the ranch's livestock, Wren begins to see past Wyatt's gruff armor to the boy who loved medicine, while Wyatt finds himself desperately wanting to protect her fragile, hard-won joy.\n\nThe Resolution & Hook: To love Wren, Wyatt must give himself permission to stop living as a ghost and finally step out from his father’s shadow. But just as he begins to believe he deserves a future, the past comes knocking. In the book’s final scene, a dusty truck pulls into the ranch driveway, the engine cuts, and Caleb—the brother who ran away ten years ago—steps out into the headlights, setting the stage for Book 2.\n\nThe author's pen name is Lillie Rose Hart. Match their typical style and expectations.\n\n--- SERIES CONTEXT ---\nThis book belongs to a larger series. Here is the series premise/bible:\nNew Project - Cowboy Romance - SERIES BIBLE — v1.0\nSERIES BIBLE — v1.0\nTHE HOLLOWAY BROTHERS OF HART'S RIDGE\nSERIES BIBLE — v1.0\n1. SERIES PREMISE & LOGLINE\nLogline: Five brothers. One ranch. One lantern that hasn't been lit in ten years.\nOne-Paragraph Pitch: In the dusty West Texas town of Hart's Ridge, the five Holloway brothers have been circling the same ten-year-old grief since the night a fire took their father, their town's legendary rodeo, and the lives they thought they were going to live. Now, one summer at a time, each brother will be cracked open by a woman who sees through his particular armor — and piece by piece, the truth of what really happened that night will come home. Steamy, small-town, trope-heavy contemporary romance for readers of Elsie Silver, Lyla Sage, and Tessa Bailey.\nSeries Tagline (Marketing): Back before the stars.\nAlternate Taglines:\nSome fires don't go out. They just wait.\nThe Holloway boys don't talk about that night. Until they have to.\n2. SETTING BIBLE — HART'S RIDGE, TEXAS\nThe Basics:\nLocation: West Texas. Roughly two and a half hours from anywhere you've heard of. Close enough to the Davis Mountains to see them on a clear day, far enough from the interstate that you have to mean to get there.\nPopulation: 1,204 (the sign has said 1,204 for eleven years; nobody has updated it)\nFounded: 1887, as a stop on a cattle drive route\nClimate: Bone-dry, wind-scoured, brutal summers, mild winters, spring bluebonnets, the occasional dust storm that blots out the sun\nEconomy: Ranching, a small oil services company, the diner, the feed store, a handful of tourists in spring who come for the wildflowers\nKey Locations:\nTHE LANTERN RANCH — Brennan family land, four generations. Northeast of town, about twelve minutes out on a county road. (Full section below.)\nTHE LANTERN CAFÉ — Maeve's diner. Main Street. Open 5 AM to 2 PM, closed Mondays. Same lantern on the sign as on the ranch gate. Booths upholstered in cracked red vinyl. Pie case visible from every seat. The unofficial town hall, courtroom, and confessional.\nTHE OLD RODEO GROUNDS — Southwest edge of town. Arena, grandstand, stables, stock pens. Has not hosted an event in ten years. The arena is still mostly standing; the stables burned and were never rebuilt. Kids dare each other to walk through it at night. Wyatt has not been inside the fence in a decade.\nDELANEY VETERINARY CLINIC — Main Street, two doors down from the café. Doc's name is still on the door. Wren will repaint it.\nMAIN STREET — One stoplight (broken since '09, functions as a four-way stop that everyone treats as a suggestion). The café, the clinic, the feed store, Sutton's Hardware, a post office, a Baptist church, a Methodist church (they do not speak), a bar called THE BRANDING IRON where Rhett bartends, a defunct movie theater someone keeps threatening to restore.\nDOC DELANEY'S HOUSE — A blue clapboard two-story on a side street, three blocks off Main. Porch swing. Rose bushes his late wife planted. Doc still deadheads them every Sunday.\nTHE HIGH SCHOOL — Hart's Ridge Combined (K-12, because the population can't justify two buildings). Mascot: the Ridgebacks.\nTHE CHURCH(ES) & THE SHERIFF — One sheriff, name Tommy Shultz, probably sixty-something, went to school with Hank, attends Sunday pot roast approximately twice a year.\n3. THE LANTERN RANCH\nHistory: Established 1889 by Eliza Brennan, a widow who inherited her husband's land claim and refused to sell it. She hung a lantern on the front gate every night to guide her ranch hands home from the far pastures. Her daughter did the same. Her granddaughter. Her great-granddaughter — MAEVE BRENNAN — married HANK HOLLOWAY in 1988 and added his name to the gate but kept hers on the deed. The Brennan women have worked this land for 136 years.\nThe Lantern: A cast-iron carriage lantern, original to the homestead. Hangs from the crossbeam of the front gate. Was lit every night from 1889 to the night of the fire. Has not been lit since. Maeve walks past it every morning and does not look at it.\nLayout:\nMain House — Two-story Victorian farmhouse, white clapboard, wraparound porch. Maeve lives here alone now. Four bedrooms upstairs (the boys' old rooms, mostly preserved). Kitchen is the heart of the house; always something on the stove.\nThe Barn — Large working barn, 1920s, recently reinforced. Hayloft. Tack room. Stalls for the working horses.\nThe Barn Apartment — Converted hayloft space above the barn's west end. Has its own exterior staircase. Small — one bedroom, small kitchen, a bathtub under a window that looks out at the pasture. Hasn't been rented in years. Maeve cleaned it herself.\nThe Horse Barn — Separate structure, newer, for the rodeo stock that survived. Jesse's domain.\nWyatt's House — A smaller ranch house about a quarter mile from the main house. Wyatt moved out of the main house three years after the fire. It's deliberately spare.\nJesse's Cabin — A one-room cabin near the horse barn. He built it himself at nineteen. Nobody goes in.\nSamuel's Cabin — On the far edge of the property, near the creek. Further than Jesse's. More deliberate.\nRhett — Does NOT live on the ranch. Has an apartment above the Branding Iron.\nCaleb — Has not lived on the ranch in ten years. His room in the main house is exactly as he left it at twenty-two.\n4. THE HOLLOWAY FAMILY\nHANK HOLLOWAY (1962–died 10 years ago, age ~52)\nThe Ghost. Rodeo legend across three counties. Built like a barn, laugh like a thunderclap, could calm a bucking bronc by humming to it. Married Maeve Brennan at twenty-six; never looked at another woman. Called his five boys \"the herd.\" Loved them fiercely and told them almost never. Had a temper he kept mostly in check. Stubborn as weather. Emotionally buttoned-up in the specific West Texas way of his generation — love was shown in actions, in showing up, in fixing things without being asked.\nSignature: Tipped his hat to Maeve every time he left the house and said, \"Back before the stars, darlin'.\"\nThe Fight: Morning of the fire, fought with Wyatt about vet school. Told him a Holloway man works the land. Wyatt said, \"I hope I never turn into you.\" Hank left without tipping his hat. It was the only time in thirty-two years of marriage he forgot.\nThe Last Words to Jesse: Pulled him aside before his ride, said, \"I'm proud of you, son. You're gonna be something.\"\nDeath: Ran back into the burning stables for the horses. Got three out. Did not come out himself.\nMAEVE BRENNAN HOLLOWAY (age ~60)\nThe Matriarch. Owner of the land, owner of the diner, owner of more information than any person in Hart's Ridge. Warm, shrewd, unsentimental in the face of sentiment. Widowed at fifty, raised five grown sons through grief by feeding them. Runs the Lantern Café six days a week and has for thirty years. Has not watched a sunset from the porch in ten years.\nAppearance: Silver in her dark hair, laugh lines, hands that are always doing something. Favors jeans and soft flannel shirts at home, an apron at the diner.\nSignature: The pies. (See Section 8.)\nThe Secret: Somewhere around Year Six, she figured out what Jesse did. She has never said a word. She is waiting for him to say it first.\nHer Authority: The boys do not fully understand that their mother is the landowner. They think they run the ranch. They do not.\nWYATT HOLLOWAY (34) — BOOK 1\nThe Dutiful One. Oldest brother. Runs The Lantern Ranch. Wanted to be a vet; wasn't allowed to finish the conversation with his father about it. Became Hank instead, on purpose, as penance.\nAppearance: 6'3\", built from labor not gym. Dark hair, dark eyes, perpetual two-day stubble. Hands that have stitched barbed wire and calved cows. Work.\nWhat Wren Sees: The boy who wanted to be a vet, still in there.\nTrope: Grumpy/sunshine + forced proximity.\nArc: From penance to permission.\nCALEB HOLLOWAY (32) — BOOK 2\nThe Runaway. Second son. Left Hart's Ridge three weeks after the funeral and became a circuit rodeo star out of Las Vegas. Famous enough that Hart's Ridge sees his face on the rare TV in the Branding Iron and pretends not to. Has not been home in ten years.\nAppearance: Leaner than Wyatt, more camera-ready, the brother who inherited Hank's laugh. Shaggier hair. Wears his buckle.\nWound: Guilt. He left. He left his mother, he left the ranch, he left the girl he loved, and he's been trying to outrun all three on eight-second rides.\nArmor: Distance. Charm. The next arena.\nTrope: Second chance romance.\nHeroine: His high school sweetheart, now a single mom. Name: Nora Henshaw.\nBook 1 Presence: Off-page until the final scene. Headlights in the driveway. Engine cut. Door opens.\nSAMUEL HOLLOWAY (30) — BOOK 3\nThe Angry One. Middle brother. Was nineteen when the fire happened and the year at college that was supposed to come next never did. Enlisted instead. Served two tours. Came home harder than he left. Lives alone in the cabin by the creek.\nAppearance: The broodingest of the five. Shorter hair, military-neat. A scar on his jaw he will not talk about. Broader than Caleb, quieter than Wyatt.\nWound: Rage he has nowhere to put. A private theory about the fire he has told no one. The thing he saw, or thinks he saw, that night.\nArmor: Solitude. Whiskey. The cabin.\nTrope: Enemies to lovers.\nHeroine: Arson investigator reopening the case. Name: Isabel Esquivel.\nBook 1 Presence: Shows up for Sunday dinner. Says maybe fourteen words the whole book. All of them matter.\nRHETT HOLLOWAY (28) — BOOK 4\nThe Charmer. Fourth brother. Bartends at the Branding Iron. Everyone's friend, nobody's problem. Lives above the bar. Looks like he's not carrying anything.\nAppearance: Golden-retriever energy, dimples, the brother who makes women laugh before they realize they're flirting. Lighter hair than the others, blue eyes from Maeve's side.\nWound: Avoidance. If he never takes anything seriously, nothing can break him. Was eighteen when the fire happened. Has never once cried about it out loud.\nArmor: The joke. The smile. The next round.\nTrope: Fake dating + one bed.\nHeroine: Caleb's disgraced Vegas ex, hiding out in Hart's Ridge.\nBook 1 Presence: Easy. Teases Wyatt about Wren within four hours of her arrival. Is always at Sunday dinner. Is the brother most visibly delighted by the Wren situation.\nJESSE HOLLOWAY (26) — BOOK 5\nThe Quiet One. Baby of the family. Was sixteen the night of the fire. Flicked a cigarette into dry grass behind the rodeo grounds trying to feel grown. Walked away. Watched his father ride. Figured out what he'd done days later, alone, in his bedroom, and never told a soul.\nAppearance: Tallest of the brothers, actually — grew late. Lean, quiet hands, dark hair always a little too long because he forgets. Moves softer than a man his size should.\nWound: He killed his father. He believes this without qualification. He has carried it for a decade.\nArmor: Silence. Work. Proximity to the animals Hank died for.\nTrope: Forbidden age-gap, friends-to-lovers.\nHeroine: His former high school English teacher, back in town. Name: Holly Lovett.\nBook 1 Presence: On-page but quiet. Six specific seed moments (see Lila's list above, Section 7 will formalize).\n5. THE DELANEY FAMILY\nDOC DELANEY (mid-60s)\nFirst name RAY. Hank's best friend since they were eight years old. Hart's Ridge's town vet for thirty-five years. Widowed when Wren was fourteen (her mother, Martha Delaney, died of cancer — off-page, long pre-series). Identified Hank's body after the fire. Has never fully come back from that Tuesday.\nAppearance: White hair, sun-wrinkled, gentle hands. Looks like a man carved out of the Texas landscape.\nRole: Platonic co-conspirator to Maeve. Sunday pot roast at the Lantern Ranch, every week, for ten years. Second father to the Holloway boys.\nArc in Series: Quiet, supportive, occasionally devastating with a one-liner at the right moment. Appears in every book. Does not die.\nWREN DELANEY, DVM (28)\nBOOK 1 HEROINE. Only child of Doc and Martha Delaney. Grew up in Hart's Ridge. Left for college at eighteen, vet school after. Worked in Dallas emergency medicine until a bad night two years ago. Quietly broke. Spent two weeks with her dad, then moved to a rental two counties over and rebuilt herself on her own terms at a large-animal practice. Now taking over her father's Hart's Ridge clinic.\nAppearance: 5'5\", curvy-soft, honey-brown hair usually in a practical braid with flyaways, freckles that show in summer. Aesthetic: Anthropologie catalog but make it manure-proof. Floral sundresses over jeans, an embroidered Carhartt, cowboy boots from Etsy that aren't quite right.\nWound: Lost a patient in Dallas after a triple shift. Family was devastated. She broke quietly over six months. Doc packed her apartment in a weekend.\nArmor: Chosen sunshine. Humming while she makes coffee. Florals with the overalls. Every bright thing is a small act of defiance.\nWhat Wyatt Sees: Not the girl in pigtails. Not anymore.\nVehicle: Beat-up Subaru Outback. Dog hair she doesn't own a dog for. Granola bars in the console. A stethoscope in the passenger seat.\n6. SUPPORTING CAST\nTHE LANTERN CAFÉ STAFF:\nGRANT — fry cook, age 50s, has worked there twenty years, says maybe three words a shift.\nBIRDIE — waitress, age 70s, knows your order, your ex, and your credit score. Calls everyone \"sugar.\" Has a running bet with herself about when Wyatt will kiss Wren. (She wins in chapter 18.)\nTHE BRANDING IRON:\nRhett tends. Owner is an old-timer named GIBBS who mostly lets Rhett run it.\nNEIGHBORS & RIVALS:\nTHE McKINNEY FAMILY — Neighboring ranch. Hank's old rodeo rivals-turned-friends. [BUILD OUT AS NEEDED — a McKinney daughter or son could surface in a later book.]\nTHE SHERIFF:\nTommy Shultz — Went to school with Hank. Sixty-something. Will matter in Book 3.\nPIVOTAL TO BOOK 2:\nCaleb's high school sweetheart, Nora — lives in town, is a single mom, per Edna's rule, kid's dad is a man who left, who we hate.\nHer child — age, gender, name TBD.\n7. THE FIRE — SERIES MYSTERY BIBLE SACRED DOCUMENT\nWHAT ACTUALLY HAPPENED, IN FULL:\nTen years ago, the second weekend of July. Annual Hart's Ridge Summer Rodeo — the biggest event of the year, the thing the town organized itself around. Hank Holloway competing, as he did every year. All five boys there. Maeve working the pie booth.\nThat afternoon, Wyatt (24) and Hank fought in the kitchen about vet school. Wyatt said the cruel thing, slammed the door, went to the rodeo angry and stayed at the arena fence drinking beer with friends.\nCaleb (22) was competing too, in his father's shadow.\nSamuel (20) was home from his first year of college, surly, not really speaking to Hank for reasons of his own (the real reasons are Book 3's reveal — he'd applied to enlist without telling anyone, and Hank had found out).\nRhett (18) was flirting with everyone and drinking beer he wasn't supposed to have.\nJesse (16) was the baby brother tagging along. Before Hank's ride, Hank pulled Jesse aside and said, \"I'm proud of you, son. You're gonna be something.\" Jesse, overwhelmed and sixteen and trying to be bigger than he was, stole a cigarette from an older kid's pack and slipped behind the stables to smoke it. He inhaled wrong, coughed, panicked someone would hear, and flicked the cigarette into the dry grass at the base of the stable wall. Walked away. Went back to watch his dad ride. Never saw it catch.\nIt smoldered for maybe forty minutes. The stable wall caught during Hank's final ride. By the time anyone noticed, the wind had it. Hank rode out of the arena, saw the smoke, and went for the horses. Got three out. A beam came down. He did not come out.\nOfficial cause: undetermined. Likely electrical (old wiring). The investigation was cursory. The town was in shock. Nobody looked hard.\nJesse realized four days later, lying in bed, replaying that night. He has told no one. For ten years.\nTHE BROTHERS' PRIVATE THEORIES (what each one secretly believes):\nWyatt: Believes the fight distracted Hank, made him ride sloppy, put him in the wrong place at the wrong time. Believes he killed his father with words.\nCaleb: Believes if he'd won his event earlier, Hank wouldn't have stayed for the later ride. Believes he killed his father by losing.\nSamuel: Saw something that night — a figure near the stables before the fire. Never identified them. Has spent ten years wondering if it was arson, if someone hated Hank enough, and if he, Samuel, failed to protect his father by not walking over to check. (Reveal Book 3: the figure was Jesse.)\nRhett: Believes nothing. Refuses to. That's the wound.\nJesse: Knows.\nMaeve: Figured it out in Year Six. A moment with Jesse, a look, something she put together. Has been waiting for him.\nTHE CONTROLLED REVEAL SCHEDULE:\nBOOK 1 (WYATT):\nEmotional reveal: Wyatt tells Wren what he said to Hank that morning.\nPlanted seeds: Jesse stopped talking for a year. Jesse doesn't drink. Jesse tends the horses. Jesse reacts to the cigarette at the test-run rodeo. Maeve watches Jesse leave dinner. The lantern is mentioned but not lit.\nBOOK 2 (CALEB):\nEmotional reveal: Caleb confesses why he really left — not just grief, but the belief that losing cost his father his life.\nPlanted seeds: Jesse's avoidance of the old rodeo grounds becomes specific. A conversation where Jesse almost says something and doesn't. Maeve bakes something unusual when Jesse walks into the café.\nBOOK 3 (SAMUEL):\nEmotional reveal: Samuel tells the arson investigator about the figure he saw that night. She investigates. The trail goes cold on paper but the reader knows. First major \"oh God\" for attentive rereaders.\nPlanted seeds: Jesse reacts when the investigator is mentioned. A near-miss where he almost tells her himself.\nBOOK 4 (RHETT):\nEmotional reveal: Rhett finally breaks. Cries about Hank for the first time. In the cry, he says something like \"I keep thinking one of us knows something and isn't saying.\" The heroine holds him.\nPlanted seeds: Jesse drinks for the first time on-page. One drink. Sets it down. Walks out of the bar. Rhett notices.\nBOOK 5 (JESSE):\nThe confession. To his teacher-heroine first. Then, in the climax, to all four brothers and Maeve. Then Maeve slides the pie across the table. \"I've been waiting, baby.\" The lantern is lit.\n8. MAEVE'S PIE LEXICON\nThe official pie dictionary. Tight list, series-wide consistency.\nPie\nMeaning\nApple\nPleased. All is well. The default.\nLemon Meringue\nSomeone's about to get their life rearranged.\nCherry\nWarning. Tread carefully.\nPecan\nGrief. Unspoken sorrow.\nKey Lime\nShe knows something you don't.\nPeach\nWelcome home.\nButtermilk Chess\nForgiveness. (The Book 5 pie. Never appears before.)\n9. SERIES MOTIFS & RECURRING ELEMENTS\nThe Lantern on the Gate — Unlit for ten years. Mentioned in every book. Lit in Book 5.\n\"Back before the stars, darlin'.\" — Hank's signature. Appears in every book. Maeve says it aloud for the first time in ten years at a key moment in Book 5.\nThe Broken Stoplight — Running gag. Fixed in Book 5. Nobody likes it.\nSunday Pot Roast — Maeve's house, every week, attendance mandatory. Every book has at least one pot roast scene.\nMaeve's Pies — every book opens OR climaxes with a specific pie call.\nThe Old Rodeo Grounds — Appears in every book. Different character goes there each time. Book 5, all five brothers go together.\nDoc's Porch Swing — Confession location. Every book has a scene on it.\nThe Empty Chair — Hank's chair at the kitchen table. Nobody sits in it. Ever. Until Book 5.\n10. TIMELINE\n1889: Eliza Brennan establishes the ranch.\n1988: Maeve Brennan marries Hank Holloway.\n1990–2000: The five boys arrive: Wyatt ('90), Caleb ('92), Samuel ('94), Rhett ('96), Jesse ('98).\n10 Years Before Series: The Fire. Hank dies. Jesse is 16.\nSeries Present (Book 1): Spring-Summer. Wyatt 34, Caleb 32 (absent), Samuel 30, Rhett 28, Jesse 26.\nBook 2: Autumn of same year.\nBook 3: Following year. Next season. Winter.\nBook 4: Following year. Next Season. Spring.\nBook 5: The next summer. Full rodeo revival — ten-year anniversary reframed as commemoration and rebirth.\n11. THEMATIC THROUGH-LINES\nInherited silence. Five sons raised by a man who loved in actions; none of them know the words.\nMatrilineal land, patrilineal grief. The ranch belongs to the women. The wound belongs to the men.\nHome as wound and healing. Hart's Ridge is where it broke and the only place it can mend.\nPenance vs. permission. Every brother has been punishing himself. Every love interest offers permission.\nThe story you tell yourself vs. the truth. Each brother has built a private narrative of that night. Love is what makes the truth sayable.\nChosen joy. Not innocence, not denial — joy as an active, daily decision. (Wren's thesis. The series' thesis.)\n12. BRAND & MARKETING ANCHORS\nSeries Branding:\nUnified cover motif: A silhouetted figure under the ranch gate, lantern hanging above. Same lantern, different brother, different heroine silhouette, book title in weathered serif. Spine features the lantern. Five books on a shelf = one lantern glowing in sequence.\nColor palette: Dusty neutrals, rust, Texas sky blue, amber. Book 5 introduces lantern-gold.\nSeries tagline: Back before the stars.\nTrope Bingo per Book:\nBook\nPrimary\nSecondary\nTertiary\n1 Wyatt\nGrumpy/Sunshine\nForced Proximity\n(father) Brother's Best Friend's Daughter\n2 Caleb\nSecond Chance\nSingle Mom\nProdigal Son Returns\n3 Samuel\nEnemies to Lovers\nWounded Veteran\nForbidden (Professional)\n4 Rhett\nFake Dating\nOne Bed\nBrother's Ex\n5 Jesse\nAge Gap\nForbidden (Teacher)\nFriends to Lovers + Mystery Resolution\nNewsletter Magnet / Pre-Order Bonus: \"BACK BEFORE THE STARS\" — A novella of Hank and Maeve, young. How they met. Their wedding. The first time he said the line. Releases between Book 4 and Book 5. Devastates everyone.\nMerch Ecosystem:\nLantern pillar candle (leather & smoke)\nThe Lantern Café recipe card set (Maeve's pies, one per book, included as special-edition inserts)\n\"Back before the stars\" enamel pin\nHart's Ridge map print\nBranded Carhartt (Wren-coded)\nTarget Reader: Elsie Silver, Lyla Sage, Tessa Bailey, Robyn Carr. BookTok-native. 25–45. Reads in series. Owns a tote bag. Will pre-order Book 2 the day Book 1 releases if we nail the ending.\n------------------------\n\n\nDo not include any pleasantries, just the synopsis text."

Here is the series premise/bible:\nNew Project - Cowboy Romance - SERIES BIBLE — v1.0\nSERIES BIBLE — v1.0\nTHE HOLLOWAY BROTHERS OF HART'S RIDGE\nSERIES BIBLE — v1.0\n1. SERIES PREMISE & LOGLINE\nLogline: Five brothers. One ranch. One lantern that hasn't been lit in ten years.\nOne-Paragraph Pitch: In the dusty West Texas town of Hart's Ridge, the five Holloway brothers have been circling the same ten-year-old grief since the night a fire took their father, their town's legendary rodeo, and the lives they thought they were going to live. Now, one summer at a time, each brother will be cracked open by a woman who sees through his particular armor — and piece by piece, the truth of what really happened that night will come home. Steamy, small-town, trope-heavy contemporary romance for readers of Elsie Silver, Lyla Sage, and Tessa Bailey.\nSeries Tagline (Marketing): Back before the stars.\nAlternate Taglines:\nSome fires don't go out. They just wait.\nThe Holloway boys don't talk about that night. Until they have to.\n2. SETTING BIBLE — HART'S RIDGE, TEXAS\nThe Basics:\nLocation: West Texas. Roughly two and a half hours from anywhere you've heard of. Close enough to the Davis Mountains to see them on a clear day, far enough from the interstate that you have to mean to get there.\nPopulation: 1,204 (the sign has said 1,204 for eleven years; nobody has updated it)\nFounded: 1887, as a stop on a cattle drive route\nClimate: Bone-dry, wind-scoured, brutal summers, mild winters, spring bluebonnets, the occasional dust storm that blots out the sun\nEconomy: Ranching, a small oil services company, the diner, the feed store, a handful of tourists in spring who come for the wildflowers\nKey Locations:\nTHE LANTERN RANCH — Brennan family land, four generations. Northeast of town, about twelve minutes out on a county road. (Full section below.)\nTHE LANTERN CAFÉ — Maeve's diner. Main Street. Open 5 AM to 2 PM, closed Mondays. Same lantern on the sign as on the ranch gate. Booths upholstered in cracked red vinyl. Pie case visible from every seat. The unofficial town hall, courtroom, and confessional.\nTHE OLD RODEO GROUNDS — Southwest edge of town. Arena, grandstand, stables, stock pens. Has not hosted an event in ten years. The arena is still mostly standing; the stables burned and were never rebuilt. Kids dare each other to walk through it at night. Wyatt has not been inside the fence in a decade.\nDELANEY VETERINARY CLINIC — Main Street, two doors down from the café. Doc's name is still on the door. Wren will repaint it.\nMAIN STREET — One stoplight (broken since '09, functions as a four-way stop that everyone treats as a suggestion). The café, the clinic, the feed store, Sutton's Hardware, a post office, a Baptist church, a Methodist church (they do not speak), a bar called THE BRANDING IRON where Rhett bartends, a defunct movie theater someone keeps threatening to restore.\nDOC DELANEY'S HOUSE — A blue clapboard two-story on a side street, three blocks off Main. Porch swing. Rose bushes his late wife planted. Doc still deadheads them every Sunday.\nTHE HIGH SCHOOL — Hart's Ridge Combined (K-12, because the population can't justify two buildings). Mascot: the Ridgebacks.\nTHE CHURCH(ES) & THE SHERIFF — One sheriff, name Tommy Shultz, probably sixty-something, went to school with Hank, attends Sunday pot roast approximately twice a year.\n3. THE LANTERN RANCH\nHistory: Established 1889 by Eliza Brennan, a widow who inherited her husband's land claim and refused to sell it. She hung a lantern on the front gate every night to guide her ranch hands home from the far pastures. Her daughter did the same. Her granddaughter. Her great-granddaughter — MAEVE BRENNAN — married HANK HOLLOWAY in 1988 and added his name to the gate but kept hers on the deed. The Brennan women have worked this land for 136 years.\nThe Lantern: A cast-iron carriage lantern, original to the homestead. Hangs from the crossbeam of the front gate. Was lit every night from 1889 to the night of the fire. Has not been lit since. Maeve walks past it every morning and does not look at it.\nLayout:\nMain House — Two-story Victorian farmhouse, white clapboard, wraparound porch. Maeve lives here alone now. Four bedrooms upstairs (the boys' old rooms, mostly preserved). Kitchen is the heart of the house; always something on the stove.\nThe Barn — Large working barn, 1920s, recently reinforced. Hayloft. Tack room. Stalls for the working horses.\nThe Barn Apartment — Converted hayloft space above the barn's west end. Has its own exterior staircase. Small — one bedroom, small kitchen, a bathtub under a window that looks out at the pasture. Hasn't been rented in years. Maeve cleaned it herself.\nThe Horse Barn — Separate structure, newer, for the rodeo stock that survived. Jesse's domain.\nWyatt's House — A smaller ranch house about a quarter mile from the main house. Wyatt moved out of the main house three years after the fire. It's deliberately spare.\nJesse's Cabin — A one-room cabin near the horse barn. He built it himself at nineteen. Nobody goes in.\nSamuel's Cabin — On the far edge of the property, near the creek. Further than Jesse's. More deliberate.\nRhett — Does NOT live on the ranch. Has an apartment above the Branding Iron.\nCaleb — Has not lived on the ranch in ten years. His room in the main house is exactly as he left it at twenty-two.\n4. THE HOLLOWAY FAMILY\nHANK HOLLOWAY (1962–died 10 years ago, age ~52)\nThe Ghost. Rodeo legend across three counties. Built like a barn, laugh like a thunderclap, could calm a bucking bronc by humming to it. Married Maeve Brennan at twenty-six; never looked at another woman. Called his five boys \"the herd.\" Loved them fiercely and told them almost never. Had a temper he kept mostly in check. Stubborn as weather. Emotionally buttoned-up in the specific West Texas way of his generation — love was shown in actions, in showing up, in fixing things without being asked.\nSignature: Tipped his hat to Maeve every time he left the house and said, \"Back before the stars, darlin'.\"\nThe Fight: Morning of the fire, fought with Wyatt about vet school. Told him a Holloway man works the land. Wyatt said, \"I hope I never turn into you.\" Hank left without tipping his hat. It was the only time in thirty-two years of marriage he forgot.\nThe Last Words to Jesse: Pulled him aside before his ride, said, \"I'm proud of you, son. You're gonna be something.\"\nDeath: Ran back into the burning stables for the horses. Got three out. Did not come out himself.\nMAEVE BRENNAN HOLLOWAY (age ~60)\nThe Matriarch. Owner of the land, owner of the diner, owner of more information than any person in Hart's Ridge. Warm, shrewd, unsentimental in the face of sentiment. Widowed at fifty, raised five grown sons through grief by feeding them. Runs the Lantern Café six days a week and has for thirty years. Has not watched a sunset from the porch in ten years.\nAppearance: Silver in her dark hair, laugh lines, hands that are always doing something. Favors jeans and soft flannel shirts at home, an apron at the diner.\nSignature: The pies. (See Section 8.)\nThe Secret: Somewhere around Year Six, she figured out what Jesse did. She has never said a word. She is waiting for him to say it first.\nHer Authority: The boys do not fully understand that their mother is the landowner. They think they run the ranch. They do not.\nWYATT HOLLOWAY (34) — BOOK 1\nThe Dutiful One. Oldest brother. Runs The Lantern Ranch. Wanted to be a vet; wasn't allowed to finish the conversation with his father about it. Became Hank instead, on purpose, as penance.\nAppearance: 6'3\", built from labor not gym. Dark hair, dark eyes, perpetual two-day stubble. Hands that have stitched barbed wire and calved cows. Wears Wranglers and work shirts, same Stetson for eight years.\nWound: Fought with Hank the morning of the fire. Said \"I hope I never turn into you.\" Has been becoming him ever since.\nArmor: Grumpiness. Silence. Work.\nWhat Wren Sees: The boy who wanted to be a vet, still in there.\nTrope: Grumpy/sunshine + forced proximity.\nArc: From penance to permission.\nCALEB HOLLOWAY (32) — BOOK 2\nThe Runaway. Second son. Left Hart's Ridge three weeks after the funeral and became a circuit rodeo star out of Las Vegas. Famous enough that Hart's Ridge sees his face on the rare TV in the Branding Iron and pretends not to. Has not been home in ten years.\nAppearance: Leaner than Wyatt, more camera-ready, the brother who inherited Hank's laugh. Shaggier hair. Wears his buckle.\nWound: Guilt. He left. He left his mother, he left the ranch, he left the girl he loved, and he's been trying to outrun all three on eight-second rides.\nArmor: Distance. Charm. The next arena.\nTrope: Second chance romance.\nHeroine: His high school sweetheart, now a single mom. Name: Nora Henshaw.\nBook 1 Presence: Off-page until the final scene. Headlights in the driveway. Engine cut. Door opens.\nSAMUEL HOLLOWAY (30) — BOOK 3\nThe Angry One. Middle brother. Was nineteen when the fire happened and the year at college that was supposed to come next never did. Enlisted instead. Served two tours. Came home harder than he left. Lives alone in the cabin by the creek.\nAppearance: The broodingest of the five. Shorter hair, military-neat. A scar on his jaw he will not talk about. Broader than Caleb, quieter than Wyatt.\nWound: Rage he has nowhere to put. A private theory about the fire he has told no one. The thing he saw, or thinks he saw, that night.\nArmor: Solitude. Whiskey. The cabin.\nTrope: Enemies to lovers.\nHeroine: Arson investigator reopening the case. Name: Isabel Esquivel.\nBook 1 Presence: Shows up for Sunday dinner. Says maybe fourteen words the whole book. All of them matter.\nRHETT HOLLOWAY (28) — BOOK 4\nThe Charmer. Fourth brother. Bartends at the Branding Iron. Everyone's friend, nobody's problem. Lives above the bar. Looks like he's not carrying anything.\nAppearance: Golden-retriever energy, dimples, the brother who makes women laugh before they realize they're flirting. Lighter hair than the others, blue eyes from Maeve's side.\nWound: Avoidance. If he never takes anything seriously, nothing can break him. Was eighteen when the fire happened. The next round.\nTrope: Fake dating + one bed.\nHeroine: Caleb's disgraced Vegas ex, hiding out in Hart's Ridge.\nBook 1 Presence: Easy. Teases Wyatt about Wren within four hours of her arrival. Is always at Sunday dinner. Is the brother most visibly delighted by the Wren situation.\nJESSE HOLLOWAY (26) — BOOK 5\nThe Quiet One. Baby of the family. Was sixteen the night of the fire. Flicked a cigarette into dry grass behind the rodeo grounds trying to feel grown. Walked away. Watched his father ride. He has carried it for a decade.\nArmor: Silence. Work. Proximity to the animals Hank died for.\nTrope: Forbidden age-gap, friends-to-lovers.\nHeroine: His former high school English teacher, back in town. Name: Holly Lovett.\nBook 1 Presence: On-page but quiet. Six specific seed moments (see Lila's list above, Section 7 will formalize).\n5. THE DELANEY FAMILY\nDOC DELANEY (mid-60s)\nFirst name RAY. Wyatt said the cruel thing, slammed the door, went to the rodeo angry and stayed at the arena fence drinking beer with friends.\nCaleb (22) was competing too, in his father's shadow.\nSamuel (20) was home from his first year of college, surly, not really speaking to Hank for reasons of his own (the real reasons are Book 3's reveal — he'd applied to enlist without telling anyone, and Hank had found out).\nRhett (18) was flirting with everyone and drinking beer he wasn't supposed to have.\nJesse (16) was the baby brother tagging along. Before Hank's ride, Hank pulled Jesse aside and said, \"I'm proud of you, son. You're gonna be something.\" Jesse, overwhelmed and sixteen and trying to be bigger than he was, stole a cigarette from an older kid's pack and slipped behind the stables to smoke it. He inhaled wrong, coughed, panicked someone would hear, and flicked the cigarette into the dry grass at the base of the stable wall. Walked away. Went back to watch his dad ride. Never saw it catch.\nIt smoldered for maybe forty minutes. The stable wall caught during Hank's final ride. By the time anyone noticed, the wind had it. Hank rode out of the arena, saw the smoke, and went for the horses. Got three out. A beam came down. He did not come out.\nOfficial cause: undetermined. Likely electrical (old wiring). The investigation was cursory. The town was in shock. Nobody looked hard.\nJesse realized four days later, lying in bed, replaying that night. He has told no one. For ten years.\nTHE BROTHERS' PRIVATE THEORIES (what each one secretly believes):\nWyatt: Believes the fight distracted Hank, made him ride sloppy, put him in the wrong place at the wrong time. Believes he killed his father with words.\nCaleb: Believes if he'd won his event earlier, Hank wouldn't have stayed for the later ride. Believes he killed his father by losing.\nSamuel: Saw something that night — a figure near the stables before the fire. Never identified them. Has spent ten years wondering if it was arson, if someone hated Hank enough, and if he, Samuel, failed to protect his father by not walking over to check. (Reveal Book 3: the figure was Jesse.)\nRhett: Believes nothing. Refuses to. That's the wound.\nJesse: Knows.\nMaeve: Figured it out in Year Six. A moment with Jesse, a look, something she put together. Has been waiting for him.\nTHE CONTROLLED REVEAL SCHEDULE:\nBOOK 1 (WYATT):\nEmotional reveal: Wyatt tells Wren what he said to Hank that morning.\nPlanted seeds: Jesse stopped talking for a year. Jesse doesn't drink. Jesse tends the horses. Jesse reacts to the cigarette at the test-run rodeo. Maeve watches Jesse leave dinner. The lantern is mentioned but not lit.\nBOOK 2 (CALEB):\nEmotional reveal: Caleb confesses why he really left — not just grief, but the belief that losing cost his father his life.\nPlanted seeds: Jesse's avoidance of the old rodeo grounds becomes specific. A conversation where Jesse almost says something and doesn't. Maeve bakes something unusual when Jesse walks into the café.\nBOOK 3 (SAMUEL):\nEmotional reveal: Samuel tells the arson investigator about the figure he saw that night. She investigates. The trail goes cold on paper but the reader knows. First major \"oh God\" for attentive rereaders.\nPlanted seeds: Jesse reacts when the investigator is mentioned. A near-miss where he almost tells her himself.\nBOOK 4 (RHETT):\nEmotional reveal: Rhett finally breaks. Cries about Hank for the first time. In the cry, he says something like \"I keep thinking one of us knows something and isn't saying.\" The heroine holds him.\nPlanted seeds: Jesse drinks for the first time on-page. One drink. Sets it down. Walks out of the bar. Rhett notices.\nBOOK 5 (JESSE):\nThe confession. To his teacher-heroine first. Then, in the climax, to all four brothers and Maeve. Then Maeve slides the pie across the table. \"I've been waiting, baby.\" The lantern is lit.\n8. MAEVE'S PIE LEXICON\nThe official pie dictionary. Tight list, series-wide consistency.\nPie\nMeaning\nApple\nPleased. All is well. The default.\nLemon Meringue\nSomeone's about to get their life rearranged.\nCherry\nWarning. Tread carefully.\nPecan\nGrief. Unspoken sorrow.\nKey Lime\nShe knows something you don't.\nPeach\nWelcome home.\nButtermilk Chess\nForgiveness. (The Book 5 pie. Never appears before.)\n9. SERIES MOTIFS & RECURRING ELEMENTS\nThe Lantern on the Gate — Unlit for ten years. Mentioned in every book. Lit in Book 5.\n\"Back before the stars, darlin'.\" — Hank's signature. Appears in every book. Maeve says it aloud for the first time in ten years at a key moment in Book 5.\nThe Broken Stoplight — Running gag. Fixed in Book 5. Nobody likes it.\nSunday Pot Roast — Maeve's house, every week, attendance mandatory. Every book has at least one pot roast scene.\nMaeve's Pies — every book opens OR climaxes with a specific pie call.\nThe Old Rodeo Grounds — Appears in every book. Different character goes there each time. Book 5, all five brothers go together.\nDoc's Porch Swing — Confession location. Every book has a scene on it.\nThe Empty Chair — Hank's chair at the kitchen table. Nobody sits in it. Ever. Until Book 5.\n10. TIMELINE\n1889: Eliza Brennan establishes the ranch.\n1988: Maeve Brennan marries Hank Holloway.\n1990–2000: The five boys arrive: Wyatt ('90), Caleb ('92), Samuel ('94), Rhett ('96), Jesse ('98).\n10 Years Before Series: The Fire. Hank dies. Jesse is 16.\nSeries Present (Book 1): Spring-Summer. Wyatt 34, Caleb 32 (absent), Samuel 30, Rhett 28, Jesse 26.\nBook 2: Autumn of same year.\nBook 3: Following year. Next season. Winter.\nBook 4: Following year. Next Season. Spring.\nBook 5: The next summer. Full rodeo revival — ten-year anniversary reframed as commemoration and rebirth.\n11. THEMATIC THROUGH-LINES\nInherited silence. Five sons raised by a man who loved in actions; none of them know the words.\nMatrilineal land, patrilineal grief. The ranch belongs to the women. The wound belongs to the men.\nHome as wound and healing. Hart's Ridge is where it broke and the only place it can mend.\nPenance vs. permission. Every brother has been punishing himself. Every love interest offers permission.\nThe story you tell yourself vs. the truth. Each brother has built a private narrative of that night. Love is what makes the truth sayable.\nChosen joy. Not innocence, not denial — joy as an active, daily decision. (Wren's thesis. The series' thesis.)\n12. BRAND & MARKETING ANCHORS\nSeries Branding:\nUnified cover motif: A silhouetted figure under the ranch gate, lantern hanging above. Same lantern, different brother, different heroine silhouette, book title in weathered serif. Spine features the lantern. Five books on a shelf = one lantern glowing in sequence.\nColor palette: Dusty neutrals, rust, Texas sky blue, amber. Book 5 introduces lantern-gold.\nSeries tagline: Back before the stars.\nTrope Bingo per Book:\nBook\nPrimary\nSecondary\nTertiary\n1 Wyatt\nGrumpy/Sunshine\nForced Proximity\n(father) Brother's Best Friend's Daughter\n2 Caleb\nSecond Chance\nSingle Mom\nProdigal Son Returns\n3 Samuel\nEnemies to Lovers\nWounded Veteran\nForbidden (Professional)\n4 Rhett\nFake Dating\nOne Bed\nBrother's Ex\n5 Jesse\nAge Gap\nForbidden (Teacher)\nFriends to Lovers + Mystery Resolution\nNewsletter Magnet / Pre-Order Bonus: \"BACK BEFORE THE STARS\" — A novella of Hank and Maeve, young. How they met. Their wedding. The first time he said the line. Releases between Book 4 and Book 5. Devastates everyone.\nMerch Ecosystem:\nLantern pillar candle (leather & smoke)\nThe Lantern Café recipe card set (Maeve's pies, one per book, included as special-edition inserts)\n\"Back before the stars\" enamel pin\nHart's Ridge map print\nBranded Carhartt (Wren-coded)\nTarget Reader: Elsie Silver, Lyla Sage, Tessa Bailey, Robyn Carr. BookTok-native. 25–45. Reads in series. Owns a tote bag. Will pre-order Book 2 the day Book 1 releases if we nail the ending.\n------------------------\n\n\nSynopsis:\nFor ten years, Wyatt Holloway has been atoning for the morning he told his father he never wanted to become him—and then watched Hank Holloway ride into a fire that stole his life and the family’s legacy. Now the eldest son runs the Lantern Ranch with a clenched jaw and a locked chest, burying his own dream of veterinary medicine under barbed wire and silence. He has no room for hope, for forgiveness, for a woman who hums while she mucks stalls. But when Wren Delaney rolls into Hart’s Ridge in a Subaru full of dog hair and stubborn sunshine, she brings the one thing Wyatt can’t outwork: proximity. The barn apartment above his livestock operation becomes her home base as she takes over her father’s veterinary clinic, and suddenly Wyatt can’t escape the scent of her floral perfume or the way she sees past his armor to the boy who once loved healing things.\n\nWren carries her own quiet wreckage—a patient she couldn’t save in Dallas, a heart she rebuilt piece by piece with defiant optimism. She’s come home to claim her father’s legacy and to prove she can still be soft in a hard world. But the grumpy rancher who glares at her sundresses and turns his back on every invitation to feel something is a challenge she can’t resist. Thrown together by a sick herd and a meddling mother, they begin an uneasy dance of mended fences and late-night veterinary calls. Wyatt finds himself memorizing the way she laughs, and Wren starts to recognize the tenderness he hides under layers of guilt. As the West Texas summer heats up, their forced partnership cracks open the graves they’ve both been tending—and Wyatt starts to believe that maybe, just maybe, he’s allowed to want a future.\n\nBut fate has a cruel sense of timing. Just as Wyatt gathers the courage to step out of his father’s shadow and into Wren’s arms, the past drives a dusty truck up the ranch lane. The headlights cut through the dark, the engine dies, and Caleb Holloway—the brother who vanished ten years ago and never looked back—swings open the door. Wyatt’s chance at love and redemption hangs in the balance, while the lantern on the gate stays dark, waiting for the truth that none of them have been brave enough to tell.\n\nFor each character, you must provide the following details:\n- name: The character's full name.\n- role: Narrative role (e.g., Protagonist, Antagonist, Love Interest, Supporting).\n- description: A general 1-2 sentence summary of who they are.\n- identity: Core occupation, background, or social role.\n- physicalDescription: Age, height, hair, build, and overall style.\n- distinctFeatures: Distinct physical markers, scars, mannerisms, or voice traits.\n- coreValues: Guiding principles and what they stand for.\n- flaws: Main psychological or behavioral flaws.\n- fears: Deepest core fears or phobias.\n- want: The Want (External Goal - what they consciously strive for).\n- need: The Need (Internal Growth - what they must learn or accept to grow emotionally).\n- lie: The Lie (The false belief they hold about themselves or the world that holds them back).\n\nFormat your response EXACTLY as a JSON array of 8 to 10 objects with the exact keys: \"name\", \"role\", \"description\", \"identity\", \"physicalDescription\", \"distinctFeatures\", \"coreValues\", \"flaws\", \"fears\", \"want\", \"need\", \"lie\".
